25:T4dc,You who believe, when you contract a debt for a stated term, put it down in writing: have a scribe write it down justly between you. No scribe should refuse to write: let him write as God has taught him, let the debtor dictate, and let him fear God, his Lord, and not diminish &#91;the debt&#93; at all. If the debtor is feeble-minded, weak, or unable to dictate, then let his guardian dictate justly. Call in two men as witnesses. If two men are not there, then call one man and two women out of those you approve as witnesses, so that if one of the two women should forget the other can remind her. Let the witnesses not refuse when they are summoned. Do not disdain to write the debt down, be it small or large, along with the time it falls due: this way is more equitable in God&rsquo;s eyes, more reliable as testimony, and more likely to prevent doubts arising between you. But if the merchandise is there and you hand it over, there is no blame on you if you do not write it down. Have witnesses present whenever you trade with one another, and let no harm be done to either scribe or witness, for if you did cause them harm, it would be a crime on your part. (TA.)    </entryFree>29:T15e7,<entryFree id="n34199" key="فِعْلٌ" type="main">     
                  <form>       
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">فِعْلٌ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form>: see 1, in two places: [as a subst. from <foreign lang="ar">فَعَلَهُ</foreign>] it signifies [<hi rend="ital">A deed,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">an action:</hi> or] <hi rend="ital">a motion</hi> (<foreign lang="ar">حَرَكَةٌ</foreign>) <hi rend="ital">of a human being:</hi> (K:) or, as Sgh says, the <hi rend="ital">origination of anything, whether it be what is termed</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">عَمَلٌ</foreign> [which means <hi rend="ital">work</hi> or <hi rend="ital">labour</hi> or <hi rend="ital">service</hi> as well as <hi rend="ital">a deed</hi> or <hi rend="ital">an action</hi>] or <hi rend="ital">other than it;</hi> so that it is more general in application than <foreign lang="ar">عَمَِلٌ</foreign>: (TA:) or it is a metonymical term for <hi rend="ital">any</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">عَمَل</foreign> [meaning <hi rend="ital">deed</hi> or <hi rend="ital">action</hi>] <hi rend="ital">that is transitive</hi> (M, K, TA) or <hi rend="ital">intransitive</hi> (M, TA:) or <hi rend="ital">a mode that is accidental to the producer of an effect upon another</hi> [<hi rend="ital">person</hi> or <hi rend="ital">thing</hi>] <hi rend="ital">by reason of the producing of the effect at the first; as the mode that ensues to the cutter by reason of his being cutting:</hi> or, as Er-Rághib says, the <hi rend="ital">production of an effect considered with reference to an agent thereof;</hi> and it is <hi rend="ital">common to that which is by his,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">its, origination or otherwise, and to that which is with knowledge or otherwise, and to that which is by intention or otherwise, and to what proceeds from the human being or the animal</hi> [<hi rend="ital">of any kind</hi>] <hi rend="ital">or the inanimate thing;</hi> and <foreign lang="ar">عَمَلٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">صُنْعٌ</foreign> are more particular in application: El-Harállee says that the <foreign lang="ar">فِعْل</foreign> is <hi rend="ital">what has become apparent in consequence of a motive of the efficient, whether from knowledge or otherwise, by reason of premeditation</hi> [for <foreign lang="ar">لِتَدَيُّن</foreign> (an obvious mistranscription in my original) I read <foreign lang="ar">لِتَدَبُّرٍ</foreign>] <hi rend="ital">or otherwise:</hi> and El-Juweynee says that it is <hi rend="ital">what is within the limits of a small space of time, without repetition,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">reiteration,</hi> whereas the <foreign lang="ar">عَمَل</foreign> is what has been repeated, or reiterated, and whereof the time has been long; but this is repugned by the trad. [in which occurs the saying], <foreign lang="ar">مَا فَعَلَ النُِّغَيْر</foreign> [expl. in art. <foreign lang="ar">نغر</foreign>]; (TA:) the pl. is <foreign lang="ar">فِعَالٌ</foreign> (S, O, Msb, K) and <foreign lang="ar">أَفْعَالٌ</foreign> [a pl. of pauc.], (O, TA,) [and <foreign lang="ar">أَفَاعِيلُ</foreign> is app. a pl. pl., i. e. pl. of <foreign lang="ar">أَفْعَالٌ</foreign>, like <foreign lang="ar">أقَاوِيلُ</foreign> pl. of <foreign lang="ar">أَقْوَالٌ</foreign> which is pl. of <foreign lang="ar">قَوْلٌ</foreign>, and many other instances]: you say, <foreign lang="ar">إِنَّ الرِّشَا تَفْتَلُ الأَفَاعِيلَ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">وَتُنْسِى إِبْرَاهِيمَ وَإِسْمَاعِيلَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Verily bribes do</hi> great <hi rend="ital">deeds, and cause</hi> the receivers <hi rend="ital">to forget</hi> the principles of <hi rend="ital">Ibráheem and Ismá'eel,</hi> who are esteemed models of true religion]. (TA. [This saying is written in my original without any vowel-signs, perhaps because well known: and it is there added that <foreign lang="ar">الافاعيل</foreign> may be pl. of <foreign lang="ar">افعول</foreign> (which has been altered by the copyist and is probably a mistranscription for <foreign lang="ar">أَفْعُولَةٌ</foreign>) or of <foreign lang="ar">افعال</foreign>; with other remarks equally doubtful and unimportant.]) [Hence, <foreign lang="ar">بِالفِعْلِ</foreign> meaning <hi rend="ital">Actually;</hi> as opposed to <foreign lang="ar">بِالقُوَّةِ</foreign> i. e. potentially, or virtually.]          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  As used by the grammarians, it means [<hi rend="ital">A verb;</hi> i. e.] <hi rend="ital">what denotes a meaning in itself together with any one of the three times</hi> [<hi rend="ital">past and present and future:</hi> but it should be observed that it includes the <foreign lang="ar">مَصْدَر</foreign>, or <hi rend="ital">infinitive noun;</hi> and also that there is what is termed <foreign lang="ar">فِعْلٌ ناقِصٌ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">an incomplete,</hi> i. e. <hi rend="ital">non-attributive, verb</hi> (as <foreign lang="ar">كَانَ</foreign> coordinate to <foreign lang="ar">صَارَ</foreign>, &amp;c.); as well as what is termed <foreign lang="ar">فِعْلٌ تَامٌّ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">a complete,</hi> i. e. <hi rend="ital">attributive, verb</hi>]. (TA.)    </entryFree>2a:T640,<entryFree id="n34200" key="فَعْلَةٌ" type="main">

                  <hi rend="ital">A single</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">فِعْل</foreign> [i. e. <hi rend="ital">deed</hi> or <hi rend="ital">action</hi>], (Msb, TA,) with fet-h. (Msb.) Thus in the saying in the Kur [xxvi. 18], <foreign lang="ar">وَفَعَلْتَ فَعْلَتَكَ ٱاَّتِى فَعَلْتَ</foreign> [lit. <hi rend="ital">And thou hast done thy one deed that thou hast done</hi>]; as though the speaker said, <foreign lang="ar">فَتَلْتَ النَّفْسَ</foreign>

                  <foreign lang="ar">الَّتِى قَدْ عَرَفْتَهَا</foreign>: so says Zj; but he adds that the former reading is better. (TA.)
